Local News 2

The National Emblem Reappears in the Four Districts of Zhabei 120

Report on the situation of yesterday's takeover

Joint committee supervises the handover. Japanese troops leave; our police take over defense. Zhabei, occupied by Japanese forces for over two months, is now being returned following the signing of the ceasefire agreement. The Japanese side has agreed to first withdraw from a portion of Zhabei, south of Suzhou Creek, west of Jinghu Road, and east of Guangzhao Road, encompassing a circumference of approximately seven li. This area comprises the Fourth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, as well as its First and Second Sub-stations. After inspecting the area the day before yesterday, our side arranged for the handover to take place at 8:00 AM on the 16th. Accordingly, yesterday morning at 1:00 AM, Police Captain Huang Ming and Fourth District Chief Wu Shaolin, along with Joint Committee member Yu Hongjun, Police Captain Huang Ming,

led police officers and the Beiping Security Team to take over. Following the takeover, the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Zhabei Office was established, and household registration surveys commenced. Takeover Committee members including Yin Rugeng visited for inspection in the afternoon. Today, personnel will be dispatched at 1:00 PM to take over Dachang, and Zhenru and Pengpu Towns are scheduled for takeover on the 20th, with the area north of the Jinghu Railway in Zhabei to be taken over on the 21st. Details are recorded separately below. ▲Departure Situation Our takeover personnel assembled at the Lianshe and departed at 7:30 AM yesterday. Simultaneously, 300 members of the Security Team transferred from Beiping, led by Commander Lu Lu, arrived at the Municipal Public Security Bureau at 6:15 AM. Together with Police Captain Huang Ming and Chief Inspector Gong Xikui of the Public Security Bureau, they departed in five patrol cars from the Bureau and ten trucks from a Chinese moving company, braving the rain. They proceeded via North Zhonghua Road, entering Minguo Road, passing Zhengjia Wooden Bridge, heading west on Edinburgh Road, turning north onto Tongfu Road in the Public Concession, entering Carter Road, and arriving at Hengfeng Road Bridge (i.e., New Sampan Factory Bridge) to meet. At 7:45 AM, they reached the Police Training School on Republican Road and began deploying defenses. ▲Supervision of Handover Public Security Bureau Chief Inspector Gong Xikui arrived at the headquarters of the 5th Battalion of the Japanese Military Police on Xinmin Road at 7:50 AM. Japanese Secretary Yin Tixin coordinated with the Japanese side, and by 8:00 AM, Director Wen Yingsheng, accompanied by neutral representatives, American Lieutenant Colonel Tranda and Lieutenant Suler, arrived at Zhabei Headquarters in one car. Japanese representatives Major General Uematsu, Colonel Sugisaka, Commander Katsuno, and others were present. Wen, along with two advisors, went out to inspect Guangzhao Road, Xinmin Road, and other areas for a week before returning to headquarters, by which time it was 8:30 AM. Officers Kohara Yu 9 and Odamura from the Japanese Military Police Headquarters handed over the inventory to our representatives for review. The inventory consisted of all items within the Zhabei Chamber of Commerce (now the Japanese Military Police Battalion Headquarters) occupied by Japanese soldiers. After inspection by our representatives, they signed the document. The inventory consisted of two Japanese books. The Japanese version was signed by Katsuno Minoru, Commander of the 5th Battalion of the Japanese Military Police, who wrote four characters (meaning "the items listed on the right are handed over") after the Japanese inventory. Below that, he wrote "May 16, Showa 7, Katsuno Minoru, Commander of the 5th Battalion of the Shanghai Japanese Naval Landing Force." Our side, represented by Police Captain Huang Ming, signed after the Chinese inventory, stating "Received without error, May 16, 21st year of the Republic of China, Huang Ming, Captain of the Police Brigade of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau." After both parties signed and stamped, the handover procedure was completed. Everyone was very pleased and took a commemorative photograph at the Japanese Military Police Battalion Headquarters. ▲Japanese Address After the handover ceremony was completed, Lieutenant Colonel Tranda congratulated both Chinese and Japanese representatives on the success of the peace. The representatives shook hands in greeting. Subsequently, Japanese Colonel Sugisaka delivered a speech in Japanese to both sides, which was translated by our Yin Tixin. He stated, "The Japanese troops' advance into Zhabei was a necessary measure to protect overseas residents. Now, due to the ceasefire agreement, we are complying with the agreement and returning the occupied area. Japan and China are neighboring countries in East Asia, and we hope to promote goodwill from now on and further increase the prosperity of Zhabei." Everyone applauded and dispersed at 9:05 AM. ▲Japanese Troops Withdraw At the sound of the military bugle, the Japanese troops formed ranks, turned north on Xinmin Road, and took Datong Road, crossing the railway to depart. The Fourth and Fifth Battalions, except for some units that had already left, numbered three to four hundred who departed yesterday morning. Three Japanese naval armored cars also cleared the way. At 9:30 AM, the Japanese troops completely left the area taken over by our side. ▲Our Police Enter Zhabei The Beiping Security Team of our side arrived in Zhabei at 7:45 AM, initially with 250 men. A portion of them, over one hundred men, gathered in front of the Republican Road Police Training School. This school had been occupied by Japanese troops as the headquarters of the Fourth Military Police Battalion. Our police officers lined up in front of the gate. At 8:00 AM, there was a sudden downpour, and the road became muddy, but the Security Team's spirit remained high and well-organized. At 9:00 AM, the Japanese troops inside the training school all left by vehicle, and the Security Team entered in an orderly fashion. ▲Situation of Taking Over Yesterday morning around 8:00 AM, Police Captain Huang Ming, Chief Inspector Gong Xikui, former Fourth District Second Sub-station Chief Han Tiexian, and Secretary Wen Tixin went to the Japanese Military Police Headquarters to notify them and discuss the details of the takeover. Shortly thereafter, Fourth District Chief Wu Shaolin led 22 police officers and 2 police sergeants, Second Sub-station Chief Han Tiexian led 19 police officers and 1 police sergeant, and Special Operations Platoon Leader Chen Zhenyi led 1 police officer and 1 police sergeant to take over Japanese posts within their respective jurisdictions. The handover procedure involved two police officers being assigned to each Japanese post, and the Japanese soldiers then withdrew. After the takeover was completed, both sides saluted each other. Police officers from the Fourth District patrolled the area yesterday. (Photo by Li Zun)

▲Designated Garrisons The other two teams of the Beiping-transferred Shanghai Security Team (i.e., the Third and Fourth Teams), totaling 250 men, were ordered yesterday afternoon to assemble on Republican Road by vehicle, led by Commander Lu Lu, to await further assignments. The temporary garrison locations for each team are listed below: The First Company of the Police Brigade is stationed at the former Shanghai North Office on Republican Road; the Eleventh Company is stationed at the original site of the former Third Company; the Special Operations Team is stationed on Meiyuan Road; the First and Second Teams of the Beiping-transferred Shanghai Security Team are stationed on Xinmin Road; the Third and Fourth Teams are stationed at the Gengxin Stage on Menggu Road. ▲Establishment of an Office The Shanghai North Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau was officially established yesterday. The Public Security Bureau appointed Police Captain Huang Ming to concurrently serve as the Director of the Shanghai North Office. At 7:14 AM yesterday, he led all staff members to the old site of the Police Training School on Republican Road to arrange everything. At 9:00 AM, after the Japanese troops had completely withdrawn, the office was officially established. The list of staff members is as follows: Lu Xuechong handles documents, Wang Wenlong and Li Fuhao are copy editors, Huang Songyu and Huang Yirong handle procurement and repairs, Yao Wenhua handles accounting, Huang Luotian handles general affairs, Zhou Dezhuo manages servants, Li Shiying handles temporary dispatches, Zhou Jiuru handles military affairs, and Wang Guang handles translation. All of the above staff members were transferred from the Public Security Bureau. ▲Household Registration Survey The Public Security Bureau limited the time for organizing the takeover area and conducting household registration surveys to yesterday, with the survey managed by Wu Hefu, Director of the Household Registration Section. (1) The First General Assembly Point was established at the Fourth District Headquarters, and the Second General Assembly Point was established at the intersection of Hengfeng Road and Republican Road (this General Assembly Point was a temporary office using a car). Two staff members were assigned to each point to direct and coordinate all survey matters. (2) The surveyors were divided into three main groups. The first group consisted of 3 staff members, 9 household registration police officers, and 26 patrol officers. The second group consisted of 2 staff members, 6 household registration police officers, and 20 patrol officers. The above two groups coordinated with the First General Assembly Point in the jurisdiction of the Fourth District and the First Sub-station of the Fourth District. The third group belonged to the jurisdiction of the Second Sub-station of the Fourth District, consisting of 2 staff members, 6 household registration police officers, and 20 patrol officers, coordinating everything with the Second General Assembly Point. (3) They assembled at 8:00 AM and immediately set out, distributing forms in the morning and collecting them in the afternoon, all returning to the General Assembly Point for organization. It was planned to complete the survey within one day. (4) 80 police officers were dispatched to assist in the process. ▲Committee Inspection At 1:00 PM, Takeover Committee members Yin Rugeng, Guo Dehua, Zhu Xibai, Han Deqin, and Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, Secretary Tang Ruxuan, and six others departed from the Lianshe to inspect the Zhabei takeover area. They first went to the Shanghai North Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for a short rest, and discussed and gave instructions to Office Director Huang Qiang on the subsequent reorganization and revitalization of Zhabei. After 2:00 PM, led by Director Huang, the committee members departed from Republican Road and made a round trip to Datong Road, Suzhou Road, Manzhou Road, Menggu Road, Wuzhen Road, and Meiyuan Road. They were pleased to see that residents had begun to move in, and many shops had opened for business, with the area being very peaceful. They then turned back by car. ▲National Flag Flying The areas under the jurisdiction of the Fourth District Headquarters and the First and Second Sub-stations, encompassing a circumference of approximately seven li, were officially taken over at 8:00 AM yesterday, after the Japanese troops withdrew. Currently, a portion of the Third Sub-station (i.e., Zhenru) within the Fourth District has not yet been taken over. Since the takeover yesterday morning, traffic in and out of the concession and Zhabei is still only possible via the New Sampan Factory Bridge. The iron gates at the Xinjiang Road intersection, Menggu Road intersection, New Zhabei Bridge, and Wuzhen Bridge have not yet been opened by the concession authorities, so passage is still not possible. Yesterday, upon hearing the news, people from all sides came to visit one after another, and many residents of Zhabei also went to inspect their homes. Many also carried furniture, suitcases, and baggage, and moved in immediately. National flags were hung in front of shops on all roads, fluttering in the wind. ▲Public Announcements to Reassure the People (1) Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Announcement, Zheng Zi No. 11, regarding an announcement: In order to make an announcement, the Japanese troops in Zhabei are now gradually withdrawing, and all withdrawn areas will be taken over by officials and police officers dispatched by this Bureau to restore the original state. The police have full responsibility for local security. In addition to ordering subordinates to do their best to protect at all times, it is hereby urgently announced to all merchants and residents that they should live and work in peace, without causing alarm or disturbance. If any lawless elements take the opportunity to spread rumors and cause trouble, they will be severely punished and will not be tolerated. They must all comply. This announcement is imperative. May 16, 21st year of the Republic of China, Director Wen Yingsheng. (2) Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Announcement, Zheng Zi No. 12, regarding an announcement: In order to make an announcement, the Japanese troops in the Zhabei withdrawal area, etc., will be taken over by officials and police officers dispatched by this Bureau. The police have full responsibility for local security. If any lawless elements attempt to cause trouble, they will be severely punished according to the law. The curfew period will be from 6:30 PM to dawn the next day, starting from the date of this announcement. It is hereby urgently announced to all merchants and residents for their information. This announcement is imperative. May 16, 21st year of the Republic of China, Director Wen Yingsheng. ▲Takeover Bulletin At 7:15 AM yesterday morning, the Takeover Committee dispatched Secretary Li Jian, Special Envoy Jin Gong, together with Public Security Bureau Chief Inspector Gong Xikui, Public Security Bureau Secretary Yin Tixin, and Police Captain Huang Ming, and others, to take over the original areas managed by the Fourth District and the First and Second Sub-stations of the Public Security Bureau south of the railway. In accordance with the agreement between the two sides yesterday, they went to take over. First, Captain Huang led 250 police officers and at 8:00 AM, they transferred to the Public Security Bureau Training School on Republican Road. After a complete takeover, they were immediately assigned to their posts. At precisely 9:00 AM, Chinese and Japanese handover personnel gathered at the headquarters of the Fifth Battalion of the Japanese Naval Landing Force on Xinmin Road. At the same time, the Joint Committee dispatched two American military attachés, and our side was attended by Committee Member Wen. The Japanese side was attended by Major General Uematsu, Colonel Matsuzaka, Lieutenant Colonel Harada, and staff members. The Japanese side prepared two copies of the inventory, with the 5th Battalion Commander Katsuda Minoru signing and stamping the Japanese copy, and the Public Security Bureau Captain Huang signing and stamping our copy. They exchanged the copies, each keeping one. Colonel Matsuzaka then said goodbye and declared the end of the handover. All stationed Japanese troops immediately formed ranks and withdrew safely. From then on, the Public Security Bureau Captain Huang was responsible for maintaining local order. All other offices of government agencies were taken over separately by personnel dispatched by the respective departments. The takeover personnel inspected the area for a week and, seeing that everything was in order, returned to the meeting to report one after another by car. ▲Takeover of Schools Yesterday, within the portion of the Zhabei area taken over, there were two municipal elementary schools and twenty-six private primary and secondary schools. The Municipal Bureau of Education dispatched Ma Chonggan, Zhong Shijie, Zhu Chenggui, Jin Baoxian, together with the principals of the municipal elementary schools, Xu Suying and Zhang Xiaotian of Yongxing Elementary School, custodians Feng Fusheng and Kong Fanxi, and other personnel to take over and inspect at 8:00 AM. It was found that the municipal Yongxing School had no major damage. The municipal Xinmin School had been occupied by Japanese troops, and all school equipment was missing, but the teachers' and staff's luggage was still there. Only empty school buildings were found at the Sanyu Primary and Secondary School, the Second Children's School for employees of the Ministry of Railways, and the Rotary School on Lianglu, and all school equipment and books had been stolen. Huangfang Elementary School lost over 1,000 yuan worth of instruments and books, and luggage was stolen. The following schools had no major damage: Zhabei, Zhenghua, Zhong'an, Renhui, Huadan, Gonghe, Xinguang, Dimeng, Beishi, Huazhi, Zhihe, Xinhua, etc. The following schools were all undamaged: Huadong, Zizhi, Ningbo Second, Qingye, Zhonghua Yiwu, Liqing, etc. The two elementary schools, Jingwen and Xingmin, suffered considerable losses. ▲Takeover of Dachang The takeover personnel for Dachang, Second District Chief Lu Fengxiang, Tao Xiaojie, and four others from Baoshan County, departed yesterday morning, first to Luodian, then transferring to Nanxiang, to coordinate the takeover procedures with Capital Security Team Leader Bian Yasan. At the same time, Team Leader Bian also dispatched Shen Jianhou, Section Chief of the Fourth Section of the Capital Police Department, to Shanghai yesterday afternoon to coordinate with the committee. For today's takeover of Dachang, Team Leader Bian decided to draw one company, totaling 100 men, from the Second Company of police soldiers currently stationed in Nanxiang, to be led by the takeover personnel, to walk from Nanxiang to Dachang, so that they could arrive in the area immediately when the Japanese troops were about to withdraw, and maintain order immediately after the takeover. After coordinating, Section Chief Shen returned to Nanxiang that evening to report. According to Yin Rugeng, the Japanese troops in Dachang are permitted to withdraw at 1:00 PM today. Our side will prepare to depart from Nanxiang in the morning, and after the Japanese troops withdraw in the afternoon, they will immediately lead the police to enter and take over. The issue of troop deployments in Pudong and the South City

Not Restricted by the Agreement 121

▲Dai Ji's Reply to Wang Xiaolai's Letter Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai, because after the signing of the Shanghai ceasefire agreement, Japanese newspapers reported that the agreement included a clause with strict restrictions on the Chinese troop deployments in Pudong and south of Suzhou Creek,

Page 10

on the 9th of this month, during a meeting, he met with Songhu Garrison Commander Dai Ji and inquired about the truth. Dai immediately denied the matter. After Wang returned to the Chamber, he translated the newspaper reports and sent them to Dai, requesting him to provide an explanation. At the time, he also telegraphed the Executive Yuan of the National Government, requesting it to announce whether there were any other secret annexes to the ceasefire agreement besides the published documents, in order to dispel the initial doubts of the public. The next day, he received a reply from Executive Yuan President Wang, stating that there were no other secret documents. The day before yesterday, he received a formal reply letter from Commander Dai, explaining that he had rejected the Japanese side's inquiry during the meeting. The original letters between Wang and Dai are as follows: ▲Wang Xiaolai's Letter to Dai Ji Commander Xiaokun, I was very pleased with our recent conversation. After returning to the Chamber, I immediately translated the news about the Shanghai troop deployment issue published in the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun on May 3rd and the Tokyo Hochi Shimbun on May 5th and sent them to you for your review. Outside misunderstandings may have arisen from this, and it seems that the authorities should provide some explanation to dispel public doubts. I hope you will consider this and respond. With best wishes, Wang Xiaolai bows, May 9th, 2:00 PM. (Attached copies) (1) Troop deployment issue published in the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun on May 3rd: The issue of Chinese troop deployment in Pudong and south of Suzhou Creek, resolved by the Military Expert Committee on the 2nd, has been completely resolved. The gist is as follows: With the consent of the Chinese representatives, it was recorded in the meeting agenda that (Chinese troops around Shanghai are not allowed to take any military action, and neutral military officers are responsible for this). The document was sealed by military officers from various countries. Regarding Pudong in front of the Yangshupu Military Headquarters, the Chinese representatives provided written proof that no troops would be stationed in that area, and that no troops would be stationed in that area until Japan withdrew its troops. The above was recorded in writing and delivered to the Japanese representatives, and the minutes of the meeting were jointly sealed by military officers from various countries. This is the point where the troop deployment issue was resolved. Furthermore, Chinese troops are strictly prohibited from entering or exiting northern Pudong, regardless of the purpose. The same newspaper also reported that regarding the ceasefire agreement, the Chinese side had stated that they would not enter or exit south of Suzhou Creek and Pudong. The Japanese military believed that regarding the opposite bank of the Shanghai Concession in northern Pudong, regardless of the purpose, the Chinese side acknowledged that they would not enter or exit, recording the term (matter of understanding). (2) The Tokyo Hochi Shimbun reported on May 5th, regarding the troop deployment issue after the Shanghai ceasefire, as follows: (Chinese troops are not allowed to enter or exit the area 20 kilometers from Shanghai, so Japanese troops should also withdraw from the designated area. This is a great success for Japanese diplomacy. On the one hand, it will further convene a round table conference in the form of a chart.) ▲Dai Ji's Reply to Wang Xiaolai's Letter Mr. Xiaolai, I have received and respectfully read your letter and the attached translation of the Japanese newspaper report. I am deeply grateful for your concern. However, the scope of this ceasefire conference was limited to the cessation of acts of war and the procedures for the withdrawal of Japanese troops. All issues of a political nature were not discussed. The government has repeatedly stated and the chief representative has assumed responsibility for this. In principle, I should not provide further explanation. However, I am in a difficult position and appreciate your attention, so I dare to tell you what I know. Regarding the sections cited in the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun and the Tokyo Hochi Shimbun, I can responsibly assert that they are completely untrue. Moreover, Vice Minister Guo has repeatedly stated that the actions of the Chinese army are absolutely not subject to any restrictions under the agreement. As for the statement that no troops are allowed to be stationed in Pudong and south of Suzhou Creek, the Japanese side has never made such a request. However, during the meeting, the Japanese side repeatedly inquired about the positions of our troops in Pudong and the South City. Because it was outside the scope of the meeting, our side refused. There is no such record in the agreement. Some people in the country do not examine the full text of the agreement, leading to misunderstandings. I hope you will use this information to correct the situation. In haste, I respectfully reply, wishing you good health, Dai Ji bows, May 13th. ▲Wang Xiaolai's Reply to Dai Ji's Letter Commander Xiaokun, I have respectfully received your reply. The Japanese newspaper reports are all fictitious. I am very comforted and admired by your public spirit and loyalty to the country. In addition to publishing the exchange of letters to correct misunderstandings and dispel public doubts, I respectfully reply by letter, hoping for your understanding. With best wishes, Wang Xiaolai bows, May 16th.

Investigation of the Guo Assault Case Yesterday 122

▲ Li Cishan and Four Others Appeared in Court　　▲ Released on Bail of 200 Yuan Each

Before the signing of the Sino-Japanese Armistice Agreement, representatives from various organizations in the city rushed to the private residence of Guo Taiqi, the Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, on May 3rd to inquire about everything. During Guo's meeting with the representatives, a conflict arose, resulting in Guo sustaining a head injury. Subsequently, eleven people, including Li Cishan, were arrested by the French Concession police, and then released one after another, as previously reported. Now, because the government believes it is necessary to investigate this case thoroughly, the Shanghai Second Special District Court Prosecutor's Office has notified the defendants to begin the investigation. The first hearing was held at 10:00 AM yesterday. Relevant parties in the case and the defendants' lawyers were present in court to be questioned. The details are as follows:

▲ Crowded Waiting Room

The hearing was originally scheduled to start at 9:00 AM yesterday, but due to the weekly memorial service held on Mondays, it was delayed and only commenced around 10:00 AM. Those summoned had already reported to the court by 8:30 AM, including Li Cishan, Yin Zhiling, Yang Rongwei, Shen Zurong, Ni Shichang, and four others. Xie Chengping was unable to return to Shanghai from Hangzhou in time and sent a telegram to his proxy lawyer, stating that he would return to Shanghai immediately to attend the hearing. However, due to the night train service between Shanghai and Hangzhou not yet being restored, he only arrived in Shanghai at 3:00 PM, and thus could not attend the hearing. The other five, Wu Gonghan, Jiang Chengda, Fan Xueqin, Jiang Yizhi, and Tian Yuanqi, were not summoned. In addition, three witnesses, the male and female servants of the Guo residence, Xu Aimei, A Ying, and Jin Sheng, also did not appear in court. The defendants' lawyers included Yu Zhongluo, Zhao [blank], and Lu Jizong, hired by the various organizations' National Salvation Joint Association, and Qu Yue, hired by Ni Shichang. Many reporters from various newspapers also attended to observe the proceedings. The lawyers' waiting room was crowded due to the small size of the room. Those who arrived later waited outside the room.

▲ Li Cishan's Testimony

The hearing was commenced by the Prosecutor's Office at 10:10 AM. Prosecutor Wu Xiaoge and Clerk Zhao Yifen presided over the hearing. First, Li Cishan was summoned and questioned about his age, address, and occupation. Then he was questioned about the May 3rd incident. Li stated that he was from Anhui, 46 years old, residing at 7 Da Tong Road, and worked as a lawyer. On that day, he went to visit Vice Minister Guo with Yin Zhiling, Yang Rongwei, and Xie Yongping. They went as representatives of the various organizations' National Salvation Joint Association, and he himself was a representative of the Lawyers' Association participating in the Joint Association. Because they frequently met with Vice Minister Guo, many of Guo's family members recognized them. Therefore, when entering, they did not present name cards. Only Mr. Yin presented a name card and handed it to the doorman, who passed it to a young maid to deliver inside. They followed in, and soon a boy came out and said that Vice Minister Guo was taking a bath in the bathroom. He asked if the guests could wait if they had nothing else to do, otherwise, they could leave. They replied that they came specially to visit and did not mind waiting. After waiting for about 35 to 40 minutes, Vice Minister Guo finally came downstairs. Vice Minister Guo entered the room and apologized for making them wait. Then, he stated his purpose to Guo, saying that he had seen in English and Japanese newspapers that the demands made by the Japanese side were quite serious, such as not stationing troops around Shanghai. Vice Minister Guo emphatically stated that he would never do anything that would betray the country and humiliate the nation. Upon hearing this, they felt relieved. At that time, the doorman again delivered name cards. Guo ordered them to be invited in. There were four people who came, three were representatives of the People's National Salvation Association, and one was a representative of the University Students' Federation. He recognized this person because he had been a representative of the various organizations' National Salvation Joint Association on the first day and had requested to see Vice Minister Guo. At that time, they asked Vice Minister Guo to show them the original Sino-English-Japanese agreement. Guo said yes. At the same time, Commander Dai Ji and Chief of Staff Huang Qiang arrived. Seeing that they were talking to Vice Minister Guo in the living room, they retreated to another living room because they were going to a meeting and needed to change uniforms. Guo then went to the room where Dai and Huang were, exchanged a few words, and then went upstairs to fetch the agreement to show them. The people from the public who came to the room kept arriving. The room was not large, and it became crowded. Not only was there no place to sit, but there was also little room to stand. The people who came later mostly stood in the corridor and courtyard. There were both men and women, but they didn't know how they came. After Guo entered the room, he stood by the mahogany round table and read the articles. The first article said, "(Stop all kinds of military actions around Shanghai)". The public was very angry about the phrase "(No troops stationed in Nanshi and Pudong)". Therefore, upon hearing the four words "(around Shanghai)", they thought that there was a particularly big problem, and suddenly there was a sound of accusation. He and Mr. Yin advised that they should not just focus on the first article "(Stop all kinds of military actions around Shanghai)" but should read the following articles. At that time, some people opposed their words, saying "(Go, go away)". Vice Minister Guo then read the English. Most of the people did not understand English, so no one understood Vice Minister Guo's English agreement. At that time, someone suddenly snatched the draft agreement held by Vice Minister Guo and went away. Then there was a sound of abuse, starting from the corner of the room. In a short while, someone threw a copper coin at his face. He only raised his arms to cover his head, hoping to avoid being affected. Prosecutor Wu asked if he knew the name of the person who first threw the copper coin. He replied that he did not know who it was and did not see who started throwing it, so he did not know the name or appearance of the person. When the fighting started, he tried hard to stop it, but no one responded. Then Guo was injured, and everyone dispersed, not knowing how they left. He asked who threw the teacup. He replied that he did not know. The situation was chaotic at the time, and it was impossible to see clearly. Moreover, he was trying to study the content of the articles and was paying attention to that, not to the other things. It is easy to recognize a few people in a room, but difficult to recognize dozens of people. It is easy to recognize acquaintances in a crowd, but difficult to recognize strangers. These people were all strangers and difficult to identify. He only saw three or four people throwing copper coins. Initially, he did not expect this to happen. He only knew after hearing the sound of the copper coins hitting things. In short, the occurrence of this unfortunate incident was due to Vice Minister Guo's bath. If they had met earlier, and he had read the articles and left, he might have been able to avoid this incident. Initially, Vice Minister Guo stood by the round table. When the draft was snatched away, he knew the situation was not good and retreated to the sofa chair, but he was already injured. He asked whether Guo Taiqi's injury was caused by a copper coin or a teacup. He replied that he did not know and would have to ask the doctor. He asked what they did after Guo Taiqi was injured. He replied that the attackers scattered. They waited in the small courtyard because he and Vice Minister Guo had a deep relationship. Now that he had suffered misfortune, they needed to hear the doctor's diagnosis to know the severity of the injury and increase his regret. Therefore, he had deeply comforted him. In short, he felt uneasy about the occurrence of this incident. Because Guo's residence was heavily guarded on weekdays, it was not easy for outsiders to enter. Because they went often, they were able to move freely. The doorman did not strictly check them because there were people inside, which led to this mess. He asked if there was anyone wearing a Zhongshan suit among the four people who entered Guo's residence. He replied no, only one person was wearing a suit. He asked who went out to call people in. He replied that they all sat in the room, waiting for Vice Minister Guo to bring the articles, and were eager to speak. No one went out. This matter was probably a misunderstanding. Because Guo had been handling Sino-Japanese negotiations and had been very satisfactory to them, he had argued strongly with the other party at the meeting. When the government announced that Vice Minister Guo was to be the ambassador to the UK, they sent a telegram to urge him to stay, fearing that successors would not be familiar with the situation or understand the matter as well as Guo, and earnestly asked him to wait until the Sino-Japanese negotiations were concluded before leaving. Later, when Guo resigned to the government, they also urged him to withdraw his resignation. When he returned from Nanjing, they were all very happy, showing their deep friendship. As for going to the French Concession police station, it was just for them to be witnesses to prove what had happened at that time. And the patrolmen came very late, about thirty minutes after the incident. Later, Vice Minister Guo ordered Secretary Deng and Xia Qifeng to go to the police station to bail him and Yin out.

▲ Yin Zhiling's Testimony

Then Yin Zhiling was questioned. He stated that he was 35 years old, from Jiangsu, residing at 517 Avenue Edward VII, and worked as a professor. His testimony was the same as Li Cishan's, except for the following differences: (1) The child who came out to answer was probably Vice Minister Guo's child, about seven or eight years old. (2) When the crowd argued about the "(around Shanghai)" issue, they had advised that they should not take it out of context and should listen to the whole article. (3) About three to five minutes after the incident, the doctor came and said that there was no major injury, that it had been washed and bandaged. (4) The police patrolmen only arrived thirty minutes later. Several reporters also arrived at that time. They had been talking to Commander Dai and others for a long time. (5) The police wanted them to go to testify about what had happened, so they went frankly. The rest was the same as Mr. Li's response.

▲ Yang Rongwei's Testimony

23 years old, from Hunan, residing at 4 Gas Fei Road, a Japanese student who returned to China after the Sino-Japanese incident. The prosecutor asked, "Did you see who actually hit Guo Taiqi?" He replied, "I don't know." He asked, "Was it one or two teacups that were thrown?" He replied, "I don't know." He asked, "After the hitting, was there one or two teacups on the ground?" He replied, "After the hitting, we all went to the opposite room to talk to Dai and Huang, so I don't know." He asked, "After the hitting, who directed everyone to leave?" He replied, "I don't know."

▲ Shen Zurong's Testimony

20 years old, from Hunan, a law student. On May 3rd, he represented the University Students' Federation to visit Vice Minister Guo. He met three other representatives on the way and went together, but he didn't know their names because they were representatives of two different groups. After they were seated, about twenty minutes later, the crowd rushed in. He did not see any of the other three going out to greet the crowd. During the assault, he quickly hid in a small door next to the living room, so he was not very clear about the situation.

▲ Yu Zhongluo's Statement

Yu Zhongluo, the defendant's representative lawyer, stood up and said, "May I ask the court, what report is this lawsuit based on?" Prosecutor Wu replied, "This case is based on Guo Taiqi's report on May 6th and this prosecutor's inquiry at Guo's residence on May 5th." Lawyer Yu said, "Is it the clerk's record?" Prosecutor Wu said, "Yes." Lawyer Yu then reported that three of the four representatives of the various organizations' National Salvation Joint Association had been summoned. Therefore, Xie Chengping, although he had not received a summons, suspected that he was summoned. Therefore, although Xie Chengping had gone to Hangzhou the day before, he had telegraphed to return to Shanghai to wait for questioning and had received a reply telegram, "(Returning immediately)". He asked the court to verify the telegram.

▲ Ni Shichang's Testimony

30 years old, from Shanghai, residing in the refugee camp at the intersection of Hed Road and Xin Zha Road, as a staff member of the camp. On May 3rd, because the camp needed a large amount of vegetables, he went to the Wang Family's vegetable garden in Fahua Town near Xujiahui to purchase vegetables to provide to the refugees. While walking on Rue Ferguson near Route Loullie, he heard someone shouting to stop. He looked back and saw that armed detectives were already beside him. When asked what was going on, they said to talk at the police station. He was then dragged into a large car and taken to the police station, which was baffling. Prosecutor Wu then summoned Li Cishan and asked, "Do you know this person?" Li said, "I have never seen this person. There was no such gentlemanly person in the crowd." (Note: Ni's clothing, a long gown and mandarin jacket, were both silk). I did not see him at the police station either. Yin Zhiling's testimony was the same as Li's. Li Rongwei said, "I hadn't seen this person before. I only saw Ni Shichang during the interrogation at the police station." Ni said that he was a staff member of the refugee camp of the Shanghai Local Maintenance Association. Pan Futang could testify and came to wait for questioning.

▲ Posting 200 Yuan Bail

After the interrogation, at about 11:30 AM, the prosecutor ordered the clerk to give the transcripts to the defendants to read and see if they were consistent, made slight requests for corrections, and signed their names separately. The prosecutor ordered them to wait for further summons. The defendants then went to post bail. The defense lawyers stood up and said that the defendants had no suspicion of anything and that they had all come to court today as summoned, and there was no risk of escape. They asked that they be exempted from posting bail. The prosecutor thought for a long time and ordered each to post a cash bail of 200 yuan. The defendants complied and posted 200 yuan bail each, obtained receipts, and dispersed. It was 12:30 PM. This case was filed for obstructing official duties, so it was investigated by the prosecutor. The police lawyers did not attend the court.

Avenue Joffre.

Two Assassination Cases at the Same Time 123

▲ Public Security Bureau Inspector Died　　▲ Real Estate Company Employee Suffered Misfortune　　▲ The Two Cases Occurred Very Close in Time　　▲ French Concession Police Paying Attention to the Two Murder Cases

At 1:30 PM yesterday, two major shooting cases occurred simultaneously in Yuan Cheng Li, Avenue Joffre, French Concession. The victims were Cao Qingcheng, the current inspector of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, and Jin Shoupei, an employee of Samsung Real Estate Company. Cao was shot three times in the head and died instantly. Jin was shot once in the back and sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. His life is still unpredictable. The details are described below.

▲ Former Party Department Officer

Cao Qingcheng, also known as Zhijian, was 24 years old, from Yangxin County, Hubei Province. He graduated from Yangxin Municipal Elementary School and had been in Shanghai for 12 years. Two years ago, he served as an officer in the Municipal Party Department and devoted himself to the labor movement. Later, he served as an inspector in the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Cao was diligent and cautious in his work and loyal to his duties, which was appreciated by the previous directors. His parents are both alive and well. His father's name is Yanwen, 70 years old, and his mother's maiden name is Hou, 67 years old. They live separately at 23 Kangti Road, French Concession, where they run a small-scale Hubei-style wonton noodle shop.

▲ One Wife and One Concubine

Cao himself lived in Yuan Cheng Li (formerly Shaoqing Li), 41 Lane 6, Avenue Joffre, French Concession. He had one wife, Jiao, from Hubei, 27 years old, and one concubine, Hu Yueying, a local, 22 years old. Jiao had two daughters, the eldest named Haisheng, 7 years old, and the second named Rongsheng, 4 years old. He also had an adopted daughter-in-law named Taosheng, also 4 years old (Hubei custom: those who are concerned about their health must first adopt a daughter-in-law). He had three siblings: the eldest brother, Maoheng, 45 years old, and the second brother, Maojun, 29 years old, were both in Shanghai.

▲ Died After Being Shot Three Times

Yesterday morning, Cao went to the bureau on time to work. After the bureau meeting, he returned to Yuan Cheng Li for lunch. After lunch, he leaned against the window to read the newspaper. At 1:15 PM, he glanced at the clock on the wall and called out to his concubine Hu, saying that it was late. He then actively got up and walked out of the alley. However, just as he reached Yongxing Lane 2, 184 Rue Galla, a young thug in a suit suddenly emerged from behind and shot Cao three times in the head, causing him to fall to the ground immediately and die with his brains splattered everywhere. Cao Qingcheng who was murdered

▲ Another Tragedy Occurred

Upon hearing the news, the French Concession police immediately sent Western detectives to arrest the suspect. They also sent Cao's body to Guangci Hospital on Jin Shenfu Road and then to the morgue of Tongren Fuyuan Branch to examine the body and report to the Second Special District Court for examination. At the same time, Cao's concubine Hu immediately invited Cao's parents and siblings to rush to the morgue to mourn the body, which was extremely tragic. Before long, the Supervision Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau also received the news and sent staff to investigate the truth of the incident. Unexpectedly, one wave subsided, and another rose again. Jin Shoupei, a native of Jiangwan who lived on the second floor of No. 25 in the same lane as Cao, was also shot by thugs at the same time.

▲ The Bullet Flew Just as He Turned Around

Jin was 33 years old and worked as an employee of Samsung Real Estate Company on Zilai Street, French Concession. Yesterday afternoon, after returning home for lunch, a friend named Xia Baosen came to visit around 1:00 PM. The two talked for about half an hour. At 1:15 PM, the friend said goodbye. Jin sent him out. The two walked and talked until they reached the entrance of the alley. They nodded and said goodbye. Unexpectedly, Jin had just turned around and hadn't taken a step when he suddenly heard a gunshot and felt the bullet hit him in the back. He fell to the ground in response. At that time, Jin's relative Wei Maomao happened to be nearby. Seeing this, he shouted loudly to catch the suspect. Guanlong police officer Qi Fengying also assisted in the pursuit. Jin Shoupei who was accidentally injured

▲ Replacing Zheng Instead of Cao

After the incident, the French Concession police received another report and sent detectives to the scene. They rushed Jin to the police station and then to Guangci Hospital. Because the injury was in a vital part of the body, his life was still unpredictable. According to eyewitnesses, the murderer was wearing blue cloth shirt and trousers. After firing the gun, he fled north. According to speculation, Cao was wearing a suit, and Jin was also wearing Western-style clothes. The two looked similar, so they were mistakenly identified by the thugs. However, according to Cao's family, Cao had a colleague named Zheng, who was always with Cao. The two also helped each other in handling official business. Since the thugs wanted to harm Cao, Zheng should also be noticed by those people. Jin was indeed accidentally injured, but in fact, he replaced Zheng instead of Cao.

▲ Police Pay Attention to This Case

Jin Shoupei's elderly mother is still alive. Mother Gu is 57 years old, and his wife Ding is 24 years old. His wife's younger sister also lives with them. Several members of the family depend on him for a living. Since the occurrence of this case, the French Concession authorities have attached great importance to it. In recent times, assassination cases have been constantly discovered in the French Concession, such as the murder of Cao Xiaoniupi on Xinxiao Bridge Street the night before last, and the recent assassination of Wang Bin, an inspector of the Garrison Command, which are enough to cause unrest in the concession. American Shipping Magnate

Da Lai Passed Away Yesterday 124

▲ At the Age of 88　　▲ Shipping All Over the World

Robert Dollar, the American shipping magnate, had been engaged in shipping in the Far East for decades. He first opened the Sichuan River shipping line, then established Sino-American cargo ship lines, and also engaged in timber business. The amount of American timber shipped to China each year amounted to tens of millions of dollars. Later, he invested heavily to buy 17 President ships from the US Maritime Commission, operating three major shipping routes: Shanghai-San Francisco, Shanghai-Seattle, and around the world. The official postal ship routes from the United States to the Far East were completely in his hands. In recent years, due to the popularity of fast ships, he invested 32 million US dollars each to build two of the largest and fastest new postal ships in the Pacific, one named Hoover and the other named Coolidge, operating between China and the United States, breaking the new record in the Far East shipping industry. He devoted his life's work to the shipping industry. In any port in the world, he had his branch offices, docks, warehouses, and other industries. In China, he also established schools to benefit the Chinese people. He traveled around the world once a year. This year, he was 88 years old and in good spirits. He still went to the head office in San Francisco to work every day. Recently, he suddenly fell ill and passed away at 1:10 AM yesterday at his residence in San Raefel, California. When the news reached Shanghai, the American expatriates were shocked. The Shanghai head office has telegraphed all branches and ships to fly flags at half-mast in mourning.

Corpses of Three Rescue Workers Discovered 127

Lu Chunhua, Chen Zude, and Pan Jiaji, three rescue workers of the 19th Detachment of the Chinese Red Cross Society (members of the Postal Workers' Union), set off on March 1st to rescue injured soldiers fighting against the Japanese in the Nanxiang area. Because our army was retreating at the time and the team members had not yet learned of it, they were captured by the Japanese army ambushed in the bamboo forest near Jiwang Temple. Their whereabouts were unknown. Recently, the corpses of Lu and others were discovered in a wasteland in Zhao Jia Nong. Their faces were rotten, and their bodies were covered with wounds. However, their clothes could still be identified. The muscles on Lu's arms were cut off with knives, and a hole was pierced through his thigh. There were also knife marks on his buttocks, which was extremely tragic and unbearable to witness. The families mourned the deaths greatly. After coffining and embalming, they were moved to the Xiao Wang Temple.

City Chamber of Commerce Letter to Wine and Vegetable Restaurants and Tobacco Exchange Industries

Encouraging the Use of Domestic Beer and Cigarettes 129

▲ Purchasing Enemy Goods of a Drop of Wine and a Puff of Smoke　　▲ Is No Different Than Indirectly Drinking the Blood and Sucking the Marrow of Compatriots

Yesterday, the City Chamber of Commerce sent letters to the wine and vegetable restaurants and tobacco exchange industry associations to encourage the use of domestic beer and cigarettes, stating: We are writing to inform you that after reading the "Talks on Resisting Japanese Goods" published in the Morning Post on the 14th of this month, which lists the reduction of various Japanese imports in the three months from September to November of the 20th year of the Republic of China compared with the same period of the previous year, the smallest reduction was 20% for cement. The second was beer, wine, sulfuric acid, molasses, dyes, etc., which could be excused as industrial products, and other products could not be used to replace them at the time. As for beer and cigarettes, they are purely consumer goods, but even after a vigorous boycott, the reduction was only 20%, which is heartbreaking to say. In recent years, the quality of domestic Yantai beer has been pure and good, and domestic cigarettes have also made daily progress, both of which can meet the needs of society. If the wine and vegetable restaurant industry and the tobacco exchange industry can introduce them to customers when they purchase them, then at this time of common hatred for the enemy, there will be no one who must buy enemy goods. This is because if one drop of wine and one puff of smoke are enemy goods, it is no different than indirectly drinking the blood and sucking the marrow of our compatriots. After reading the report, this chamber of commerce cannot help but feel sentimental. Therefore, we specially send this letter to you, hoping that you will relay it to all members and earnestly pay attention to actively promoting it. We look forward to your attention.

Record of the Shareholders' Meeting of the Four Seas Insurance Company 131

The British-owned National Marine Insurance Company at No. 17 Bund in this city, organized by prominent Chinese and foreign business leaders in Shanghai, is registered with the government with a registered capital of ten million taels of silver and a paid-up capital of three million taels. It specializes in various types of insurance such as life, fire, and automobile insurance. With its headquarters located in Shanghai, it provides prompt service and thorough handling, ushering in a new era in the history of insurance in Shanghai. It is reported that the company convened a shareholders' meeting at 4:00 PM on the 9th of this month. Shareholders representing 122,661 shares were present. Mr. Beale, the current Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council, was elected as chairman. He reported on the company's operating surplus for 1931 and the company's assets and investments, stating that the assets of the Four Seas Company currently exceed 4.18 million taels. One million taels have been allocated as capital for the life insurance department to directly protect policyholders' investments, and two million taels serve as collateral for the benefits of other types of insurance policies. The remaining one million and one hundred thousand taels are used for the most stable and reliable investments. Therefore, those who insure with the company have not only the guarantee of legal reserves but also the entire assets of the company as a second layer of security. Since the insured currency varies from place to place, the investment of reserves also varies accordingly. Thus, no matter what changes occur in the world economy, the Four Seas Company will not be affected, its foundation is solid, and it is as secure as a rock. All shareholders accepted this without objection. Subsequently, new directors were elected, and the meeting adjourned.

Wife Suffers from Mental Illness

▲ Friends Knocked on the Door for a Long Time But Received No Response

▲ Broken Bowls and Plates Found on the Floor

Zhang Fu, a local resident, and his wife, Zhang Wu, lived at No. 392 Chongqing Road, Xinzha. On the night of the 13th, Zhang was seen as usual. Unexpectedly, on the 14th, Zhang's friend Wang Genfu went to Zhang's house to invite Zhang to go shopping in the French Concession but found the door tightly closed. After knocking for a long time without any response, Wang initially thought that Mr. and Mrs. Zhang were still sound asleep, so he did not disturb their good dream and went alone. However, when Wang visited again at 4:30 PM on the same day, the door was still closed, and there was no response to his calls. Suspicions arose, and he rushed to report to the Chinese constable on duty at station No. 2592 nearby, who in turn reported to the Xinzha Police Station. The police chief immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to Zhang's house, who managed to open the door and enter. They first saw Zhang Fu lying on the floor, with multiple injuries all over his body. He had already died. Zhang Wu was lying on the bed, also injured. In addition, broken bowls and plates were scattered all over the floor. The detectives immediately carried the deceased to the forensic station on Fielun Road for examination, while the woman was sent to the hospital. Doctors confirmed that she was suffering from mental illness. Yesterday morning, the police escorted the woman to the First Special District Local Court. According to the police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, the deceased was beaten to death, and the defendant is suspected of murder. He requested that further investigation be conducted after the examination. Judge Feng briefly questioned her and ordered the defendant to be detained for further interrogation. After a while, the special court prosecutor went to the forensic station to examine the body and questioned the Chinese and foreign detectives about the circumstances of the incident. He then ordered the deceased's family to sign a guarantee, claim the body, and prepare it for burial.

Drunkenly Stabbing Wife and Aunt 136

Aunt Sacrifices Her Life

▲ Claims to Be Mentally Confused and Accidentally Injured Aunt

▲ Mother-in-Law Testifies in Court, Saying Son-in-Law's Conscience Is Very Vicious

Ding Xingzi from Yangzhou, angered by his wife, Mao Guiying from Hubei, having an affair with a certain adjutant, locked the door of the attic at No. 195 Dongyouheng Road at noon on the 3rd of this month while drunk and stabbed Mao Guiying in the forehead and other parts of her body. At the same time, Ding's aunt, Gao Xushi, also known as Xu Huiqing, and his mother-in-law, Mao Gao, tried to mediate and were stabbed. Xu Huiqing, who had been trying to reconcile the situation, suffered eight stab wounds to her abdomen and died despite being sent to the hospital for treatment. Ding Xingzi was detained by Liu Zhaonian, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou Police Station, and was brought before the First Special District Court for a second interrogation. The details have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong presided over a further hearing in Court No. 1 of the High Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that relatives of Gao Xushi had arrived from Hankou and requested to be questioned. According to Mao Xushi, the deceased was her younger sister, whose husband had passed away. She had only one daughter named Jin Yu, who was also present in court. Jin Yu stated that she was twelve years old, had been living in Hankou, and that the deceased was her mother, who was killed by Ding Xingzi. She demanded justice. When questioned, Ding insisted that he stabbed Mao Guiying because she wanted to abandon him and follow someone else. He was so angry that he used a knife to stab her, but he only intended to scare her. He was mentally confused at the time and accidentally stabbed his aunt, Gao Xushi, to death. This was an impulsive act, not premeditated, and both knives were found in the attic, not brought from elsewhere. He spoke calmly, sometimes closing his eyes and lowering his head, and claimed that he usually did not like alcohol. According to his mother, Ding Wu, she had been living in Hankou for many years, relying on her eldest daughter to make a living. She did not run a brothel, but her daughter died last year. Ding Xingzi brought his nephew, a girl named E'zi, thirteen years old, his grandson, Xiao Mao, four years old, and a nineteen-year-old woman named Lao San, who is now on the run, to Shanghai. She now requests to take her niece and granddaughter back to Hankou. The court asked Ding if he agreed to his mother's request. He replied, "I agree." According to his mother-in-law, Mao Gao, she had spent a lot of money on the defendant, but he had a very vicious conscience and suddenly committed this act. Those who drank with him at the time were her fellow villagers with the surnames Leng and Hu, who had bought a catty of wine together. He only drank one cup and was not that drunk. One of the knives was not from the room, and he deliberately committed this malicious act. The court asked where the Leng and Hu were currently working. She replied that they were working in a fruit shop on Guangdong Street. Judge Shen ordered the case to be rescheduled for further testimony and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody.

Free Talk

A Discussion of the Recent Situation in Geneva (Part 1) 142

— Ji Ping

Mr. Wu Kaisheng, the head of the Chinese delegation to the League of Nations and the Minister to Switzerland, recently returned to China from Geneva. On the morning after his arrival in Shanghai, he met with a reporter. Despite having just finished a long journey, he spared ten minutes from his busy schedule to speak with me about fragmented information regarding the League of Nations. After reflecting on it, it seemed to have some value in recording. He said: "I have been stationed there for three years. If I were to rely on these three years of experience to report on the ins and outs of the League of Nations in their entirety, it would not be possible to exhaust the subject in a short time. I plan to write a special book after completing my official duties in Beijing, taking two or three months to allow my fellow countrymen to understand its inner workings. For now, I will first casually mention some trivial matters about Geneva, hoping to amuse the readers." The Sino-Japanese incident actually caused such a serious dispute. After the League of Nations accepted the case, it considered it the first major case of its kind that it had ever encountered. The League of Nations has already exhausted its wisdom and efforts and endured many hardships. But how effective can it be in reality? According to my observations, the League of Nations' handling of the Sino-Japanese incident can be roughly divided into three periods: (1) At the beginning of the September 18th Incident, the League of Nations did not receive detailed reports and did not fully understand the truth of the incident. Until the Paris Conference in mid-October, it was in a period of hesitation. (2) From the Paris Conference to the January 28th Shanghai War, the Japanese diplomatic representatives stationed in Europe gathered in Paris and concentrated their diplomatic power. On the one hand, they used various methods to contact the Paris press and used propaganda policies to change public opinion. The representatives of various countries were dazzled, as if they were in a fog. As a result, the Paris Conference was beneficial to Japan, and the League of Nations was in a period of being deceived. (3) With the outbreak of the January 28th Shanghai War, Japan launched a large-scale army, navy, and air force, implementing military coercion. Fortunately, my loyal 19th Route Army and 5th Army fought valiantly, holding out for more than a month. Although they unfortunately retreated to the second line of defense, the hostile actions of both sides still existed. As a result, all industries were suspended, and the interests of various countries in China were greatly damaged. World public opinion rose up against Japan, and the parliaments and powerful mass organizations of various countries criticized Japan, and the anti-Japanese atmosphere became increasingly intense. It was truly a matter of popular indignation, and Japan's ambition to destroy the covenant, invade territory was exposed to the world. The League of Nations changed its past attitude and turned to a period of condemnation. Since Mexico recently joined the League of Nations, there are a total of 55 member states. Based on factual observation, the attitude towards China can be roughly divided into three groups: (1) Those who express absolute sympathy account for eight-tenths; (2) Those who are ambivalent account for about one-tenth; (3) Those who do not express sympathy account for one-tenth. However, these eight-tenths of the countries are all weak nations. Generally, weak nations hate imperialism's violation of other people's sovereignty and territory, and they are rich in friendly sympathy towards us. The impassioned speeches of the representatives of various small countries in the previous meetings can prove this. The other two-tenths, however, are all powerful countries with very strong power. Although small countries are more numerous in number, they are actually at the mercy of others. Although they want to uphold justice, they cannot do anything about the obstruction of powerful countries! The reason why my country has never been protected by international conventions, despite Japan destroying the covenant, infringing upon our sovereignty, and seizing our territory, is because of these evil forces at work.

Biography of Battalion Commander Li of Taishan 143

— Qu Chang

His given name was Rongxi, his courtesy name was someone. He was from Taishan, Guangdong. He was honest and had a sense of propriety, yet he was approachable. In his youth, he studied in the Eastern Neighbor (Japan) and had a high reputation. He graduated from what is called the Army Military Academy, surpassing his peers. The Japanese cheated us Chinese people and often kept their secrets, but he explored them by all means. The Japanese feared him. After returning to China, he thought about making contributions to the authorities, but they did not listen. Disappointed, he joined a certain unit and then rejected everything, focusing solely on managing the army with his savings. Later, he was transferred to the 78th Division of the 19th Army and promoted to battalion commander. In the autumn of 1931, he was ordered to go to Jiangxi to suppress the Red Bandits and achieved significant military success. In the winter, he came to Shanghai. Enemy ships were continuously coming and going at sea. Knowing that there was going to be a change, he warned his subordinates to prepare for war. In January 1932, the incident occurred. He inflicted heavy damage on the enemy several times. On February 13th, the enemy launched a large fog and secretly crossed the Wenzao浜 with several thousand troops, attacking our Caojiaqiao fortress. He was the first to detect it and ambushed their vanguard, crushing it. Afterwards, more and more enemies came. He fought to the death and shouted: "If we do not defend this, there will be no Wusong! I will not rest in peace and will not let an inch of land fall into the hands of the enemy!" He fought hand-to-hand combat four times before our reinforcements were able to arrive and win a complete victory. However, he died from his severe injuries. More than three hundred people died with him.

Wang Quchang said: "Our country started sending young people to study military affairs in the East and West overseas during the Tongzhi period of the Qing Dynasty. For the past sixty years, millions have been spent annually, amounting to thousands of people before and after. But seeking those who can live up to the country, I have found two people. One is Brigade Commander Han Guangdi, and the other is this one. Guangdi died in defeat, while this one died in victory. This one seems to have surpassed Guangdi. He managed the army strictly and shared food, drink, life, and death with the soldiers, having the demeanor of an ancient famous general, but his merits ended here. Alas."

World Snippets 144

— Hai Ke

A Young Strongman

In Birmingham, England, there is a twenty-year-old young man named John Sharpe who can be considered one of the strongest men in the world and deserves the title of (Modern Samson). He is a carpenter's assistant. Whenever he has free time, he practices boxing and kicking for his own amusement, without any intention of pursuing hygiene or physical exercise. He is six feet three inches tall and as strong as an ox. He can lift a horse and a cart. He can carry six grown men on his back. His teeth can lift a very heavy wrought silver box. He can also lift from the ground an iron beam that requires two horses and a large cart to carry. Such divine power is truly amazing. According to him, (I usually like to carry things. I started playing with them at the age of six, learning to be a strong man. At the age of fifteen, I could lift a cloth-rolling machine with one hand. At the age of seventeen or eighteen, I could hold a large fruit bowl from the kitchen high, with my whole family sitting on it.)

Shad from Fuyang 145

— Zheng Yimei

Cooking fresh delicacies in early summer, shad is an exquisite dish. Shad is flat and long in shape and silvery white in color. However, the meat contains many fine bones. This is why the ancients said that shad has many bones and crabapple has no fragrance, which is considered a regrettable thing. The scales contain a lot of fat, so chefs usually do not remove the scales when preparing shad. They cut pork lard and ham into small pieces, place them on top, and then cover them with net oil. Steamed to perfection, the taste is absolutely delicious. This year, the price of shad is quite expensive, about 2,000 cash per catty. Poor scholars dare not taste the new delicacy. Shad from Fuyang is considered the best, along with bream from the Yi River, carp from Luoyang, and shad from Songjiang, all of which are famous products. It is said that the people of Fuyang say that every year during the season, fishermen catch it with nets. They must first offer it to the local magistrate. This custom has continued to the present day. Becoming an official allows one to enjoy a special culinary privilege, which is truly enviable. Moreover, it is said that shad that pass under the fishing platform of the hermit Yan Gao have a slightly red spot on their lips, resembling a light blush of rouge, which is considered a special sign. Mr. Chiang Kai-shek and his wife once boated on the Fuyang River one year and enjoyed drinking wine under the moonlight. The boatman, being perceptive, presented a shad with a red spot to replace the Han Shu to accompany the wine. Mr. Chiang did not dare to eat it immediately. Madam Soong Mei-ling tasted it first and encouraged Mr. Chiang to eat it. They both praised it endlessly. This year, the National Government has moved to Luoyang. I wonder if Mr. Chiang, after cooking carp, will also remember the shad of Fuyang. I admire his leisure and elegance.

A Record of a Returned Jade 146

— Te

Someone in Berlin received a package at their home one day. In an instant, the person who delivered it was gone. Upon opening it, it turned out to be a money pouch with the name and address of the recipient on it. It was an item lost eight years ago. At the time of the loss, it contained fifty-five marks (approximately two pounds and fifteen shillings in English currency). Now, it had increased to seventy-five marks (approximately three pounds and fifteen shillings in English currency). A note of thanks was attached, which roughly stated that the person who had picked up the lost pouch had obtained fifty-five marks and had used them to make a profit, receiving many benefits. They were now specially returning an extra pound to fulfill their wish and express their gratitude. In October 1918, a German soldier named Lutz died in battle in France. Later, a British soldier found a diary in his pocket, along with an Iron Cross medal. He carefully preserved them, intending to return them to Lutz's family. However, the diary only contained the name and no address, making it impossible to trace them. One day, while reading a newspaper, he saw that a famous German actress named Lutz Anni was performing in England. This stirred up old memories, so he wrote to her to inquire, attaching a portrait of Lutz from the diary. Although Anni was not a relative of Lutz, she recognized him at first sight and provided the address of Lutz's family. Thus, the diary and the Iron Cross medal were returned to Lutz's family after fourteen years from the date they were found.

Note: Both of these are recent events. Both involve people of good faith and can serve as an example to the world. The latter is especially commendable, as the British soldier had no obligation to return the items but ultimately did so. As for picking up money and returning it with interest, the act is certainly good, but there is still a hint of luck involved. However, the fact that the lost pouch was carefully stored for eight years suggests that the intention to return the money was not a temporary impulse. Being overly critical would be detrimental to the principle of fairness and forgiveness.

Tidi Xiangzhai's Casual Chats [Likely the Title of another column or section]

Yang Qi (Part 1) 148

— Gan

Yang Yunshi is known in the world as a poet. It seems so, but not entirely. Yunshi's original name was Zhaoqing, later changed to Jianying. After the age of forty, he changed his name to Qi. He was from Changshu, Jiangsu. He was the son of Xinbo, a Censor of the Qing Dynasty (Chongyi). He passed the combined Gengxin examination and served as a Section Chief in the Postal and Telegraph Department. He was appointed Consul-General to Singapore. He loved the beauty of the South Seas and considered establishing a business there for long-term residence. At that time, the islands of Southeast Asia were competing to plant rubber trees. Qi was interested and returned to China, selling property to obtain some capital, but it was not enough. He raised funds and leased 12,000 acres of land to establish a rubber planting company. The mountains and forests were vast, rarely traversed by people since ancient times. Dense trees blocked the sky, and brambles covered the ground. Qi would personally enter the mountains to supervise the work, unafraid of tigers, wolves, snakes, and vipers. Over a year, he planted approximately 3,000 acres of rubber trees, totaling 190,000 saplings, achieved through numerous hardships and dangers. He intended to abandon officialdom for business, hoping to live out his days in prosperity. However, with the outbreak of the European War, rubber prices plummeted. Qi's business remained stagnant for three years, overgrown with weeds, and he lacked the funds to pay the land taxes. The government confiscated the land as per regulations. Qi returned dejectedly and lived in seclusion in his hometown. Chen Xiufeng (Guangyuan), the Military Governor of Jiangxi, heard of his talent and invited him to Nanchang. Upon arriving, Qi did not wish to stay long. Coincidentally, Guangyuan sent troops to attack Zhang Zongchang, fighting in Yuanzhou. Someone cited Qi's poem "Feeling Autumn," with lines such as "White bones like mountains, generals esteemed; gold fills the land, the boatmen worry," suggesting it criticized Guangyuan's warmongering and greed. Guangyuan did not understand, seemingly believing it, seemingly not. Qi left in anger. That year, Wu Ziyu (Peifu) respectfully invited him to join his staff, treating him with great hospitality. Qi once wrote in a reply to Wu's wife, "In three years, I chose a wife and found you; in ten years, I chose a master and found Wu." He successively served as the chief of the confidential department and secretary-general, strategizing behind the scenes, knowing everything and saying everything. During Peifu's resurgence, when the army was stationed in Wuhan, a staff member, Zhang Ziwu (Qihuang), proposed diverting the Yangtze River. Qi strongly opposed it, and the plan was abandoned. The path to Pingdeng and Dengwei almost became deserted. The Seven-Li Shantang was desolate. No one paid respects at the tomb of Zhenniang. Even the Lingering Garden, the West Garden, and the Lion Grove were not as lively as in the past.

The Shanghai Incident had just begun. Shanghai residents flocked to Suzhou and Hangzhou to seek refuge. By March 2nd, after our army changed its strategy, Suzhou became an important rear base and a focal point for the Japanese army. Rumors spread rapidly, and people were in a state of anxiety. Wealthy families relocated one after another. Consequently, those who had fled from Shanghai fled again. Recently, as the situation gradually stabilized, those who had fled from the county returned one after another. The chaotic exodus came to an end.

Due to the large number of refugees, train services were disrupted. The businesses of various shifts in Suzhou were three times more profitable than usual. In this time of national crisis, all industries were in decline except for transportation, which thrived more than ever. One could say it was a blessing in disguise.

There are seven theaters in Suzhou. They had temporarily suspended performances due to the tense situation. The Eastern, Great Brightness, Lequn, Park, YMCA, and Nanjing theaters have now resumed operations. However, the Peking opera at the New Stage is still suspended due to the impact of the situation. Even the six theaters that have resumed operations have seen a significant decrease in business compared to the past. All the managers are lamenting endlessly. This is also a gift from the Japanese army.

Short News 149

— Jin

Mr. Huang Jinrong and Mr. Cao Youshan, last autumn, sent over nine hundred people to Dr. Fang Shenyu, a gold needle specialist, for diagnosis. All were told they needed no medicine. What day is this? There must be an alarming increase in epidemic diseases. Dr. Fang was deeply worried, and Mr. Huang and Mr. Cao also urged him not to stop helping people and saving lives. Therefore, they joined forces with the renowned doctor, Mr. Wang Shaoda, to establish the Quansheng Medical Society at No. 27 Hele Lane, Xinzha Road. They began providing medical services on May 9th. This is in response to the current needs, so we are happy to report it.

Mistaken Match 150

—

A certain Minister had a daughter and was very picky about choosing a son-in-law. The son of one of his friends returned from overseas, a handsome young man. The Minister liked him and said, "He could be my worthy son-in-law." A colleague heard this and passed the message to the young man, who wished to meet the daughter. They arranged to meet in a park. On the appointed day, the Minister's second wife, accompanied by his daughter, went richly adorned. The young man saw them and was smitten. He told his friend, "The tall and graceful one is truly my wife." The friend exclaimed, "That is the Minister's wife! The stout one standing beside her is his daughter." The people of the capital heard of this and found it strange, saying, "The son-in-law has fallen for his mother-in-law!" Alas!

Records of the Double Buildings in Times of War (54) 151

— Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter 7: Seeking audience at the powerful gates often makes generals falter; imprisoned in the prison of love, the jailer can be a husband.

However, Liang Xiaoyun was also very clever. Like a startled swan, she busily ran to the side of the Fifth Madam, sitting down close to her heels. She cleared the left side of the lamp stand. Ye Zuozhang had already walked to the front of the bed, blocked by the Fifth Madam, and was too embarrassed to continue chasing Liang Xiaoyun. He had no choice but to lie down on the bed as well. That day, Ye Zuozhang was wearing a long robe and mandarin jacket. He then shook off his shoes and threw them far away, raising his feet high and resting them on the bed rail, squinting at Liang Xiaoyun and laughing incessantly. Liang Xiaoyun remained calm and tried her best to appear generous and composed. The Fifth Madam spoke for her again, saying, "My eighth sister and I have been talking for a while. The person she married is from the same province where you are the Military Governor. He is a very good young student, but he also trained in the militia back home and is good at military affairs. I think, aren't you in need of people right now? Since I have such a good brother-in-law, why should I let him seek a job elsewhere? One day, please have my eighth sister bring him to meet you, and you can assign him a good position." Ye Zuozhang suddenly kicked his leg and sat up, laughing loudly, "Very good! He is my citizen, willing to come to me for a job. Of course, he doesn't oppose me or curse me. Why wouldn't I welcome him? Besides, considering Old Eighth's face, we're practically relatives. Easy to handle. Tell him to come! There are plenty of titles like Councilor and Advisor. Let him choose whatever he wants. I can even issue an official order today. That's how straightforward I am." Liang Xiaoyun had just stood up and said softly, "Thank you for the Military Governor's cultivation," but unexpectedly, the Fifth Madam reached out and pressed Liang Xiaoyun back down, her cherry lips about to utter words of disdain, "What did you say? Councilor and Advisor? Those are all worthless nominal positions. You can use them to placate irrelevant people, but for me and Eighth Sister? How can you be so dismissive? That won't do. You can't make us lose face like that. It has to be a real position! I heard that my brother-in-law has many militiamen under his command who can fight well. You can reorganize them into a regular army, which will be better than those useless officers of yours when they go to the front lines. You should appoint him as a commander and let him help you properly. You don't have to worry about not winning battles in the future. You have to be clear that most of this is for your own benefit!"
