New Silkworm Cocoons in Chang'an Only One-Third Harvest 159

▲ Cocoon prices up to 35 yuan... Farmers dry and reel silk themselves.

In the market towns near Chang'an, only 30-40% of farmers raised silkworms this year compared to previous years. The silkworm ants also suffered damage due to the weather. The new cocoon harvest is only about one-third of a normal year. Only two or three cocoon shops opened for weighing. Purchasing goods is unusually rigorous. The highest price for improved seed cocoons is only 35 yuan, and the ordinary price is 27-28 yuan. Farmers who suffered excessive losses on silkworm costs mostly carry back to dry the cocoons themselves and reel local silk, it is said.

Yesterday, the Japanese silk market in this port completely stopped because the European and American markets recently have had increasingly abundant arrivals of Japanese silk, and the stockpiles are filled. They dislike that the prices for factory raw silk etc. are too expensive and do not move. Silk telegrams are not seen turned, the market atmosphere is stagnant, and no current silk transactions are heard of, it is said.

Tea Market Situation Not Good 161

▲ Qimen Black Tea Not Yet Opened

▲ Zhenmei Green Tea Prices Continue to Fall

Yesterday, in the foreign tea market of this port, the new Qimen black tea had a huge amount of over 8,000 boxes of new samples laid out throughout the city. Recent Qiwu Tea News 162

▲ Qicha affected by excessive rain and lack of foreign demand

The new teas with the first name from all tea firms in Qimen have already arrived in Qi, and the second and third gangs are in the process of searching for them. Each firm is rushing to produce and transport them to Shanghai to grab market share, and they have all begun to pick and bake them this week. The first name tribute tea can be formed into piles within days, and the first name box tea can also be shipped within ten days. Because Qiupu has convenient transportation, the new tea can arrive in Shanghai earlier. According to Qicha merchants, the second and third name teas in Qifuqiu are not produced well due to the cold and rainy weather, and the quality and taste are lower than the first tea. For the sake of protecting costs, Hao Fang is not very enthusiastic about importing them, and the market is also declining to 30 to 40 yuan per dan compared to the first tea. In addition, the tea warehouses stationed in Qi have tightened their remittances, and the amount of loan funds issued has decreased by more than one million yuan compared with last year. In addition, the current silver in Jingtun is not accessible due to the bandits, and the Hao Fang is hindered by economic difficulties, resulting in its inability to increase the amount as much as possible. Fortunately, the number of tea firms has not decreased this year, and the mountain households have not yet been affected.

▲ Wuyuan tea firms are preparing to leave Zhuang

The new tea in Wuyi has been opened by mountain households for several days. However, due to continuous rain and cold weather, the development of mountain and island tea is uneven, and the harvesting and baking are extremely laborious, resulting in reduced shipments. Each firm is deeply afraid that the Tunxi numbers will rush to order first when the new tea is about to enter the market, and they have been preparing to leave Zhuang. The difficulty they feel is that the finance is unusually tight. As of now, none of the tea warehouses stationed in Wu have released a single ticket. All the numbers currently preparing hold self-funded activities, and Tun and Jing rely solely on a small amount of supply from local shops in this county, which is of no help. It is expected that the pain of the current silver being insufficient will be felt when the new tea opens.

If the road to the present and tomorrow is still prosperous, there is still a possibility for the market to rise higher. The total market opened with 22,000 bags of small twisted rice, priced at 10 yuan, 6 jiao, and 2 fen to 10 yuan and 3 jiao. Old small twisted rice was 10 yuan, 2 jiao, and 4 fen to 10 yuan, 1 jiao, and a half. Rough small twisted rice was 1,000 bags, priced at 9 yuan and 6 jiao to 9 yuan and 3 jiao. Saigon No. 1 was 1,000 bags, priced at 11 yuan, 7 jiao, and 3 fen. Mindang rice was 1,000 bags, priced at 11 yuan to 10 yuan, 9 jiao, and 3 fen. Another 2 weeks of delivery was 1,000 bags, priced at 11 yuan. Kaladi rough road goods were 1,000 bags, priced at 9 yuan and 8 jiao, it is said.

Flour Market Transactions Very Active in This Street 165

Yesterday, the flour market showed improvement again. Old brands were highly sought after by domestic buyers on this street, and the market immediately tightened. The month opened at 2.04 taels, quickly rising to 2.05 taels. There were orders for 1 million bags of "Warship" brand flour for this month, and the warehouse receipts needed to be collected by the 20th, causing buyers to hesitate. The opening price was 2.035 taels, and the closing price slightly decreased to 2.03 taels. "Fortress" brand was only 2.15 taels. Other brands were rarely available on the market. Returned warehouse receipts were mostly around 2.05 taels, it is said.

Raw Granulated White Sugar Tends to Decline Again 166

Yesterday, the sugar market at the guild was weak, resulting in scattered transactions. Initially, the seller's asking price for No. 24 Dutch sugar (raw granulated white) was 13.35 taels, but there was little interest. Later, the transaction price fell to 13.275 taels, and buying interest remained low. Sellers were still active, and the market was generally quiet, with a downward trend. Medium granulated white sugar was even less in demand. Transactions of Taikoo sugar were also sluggish. Tianjin B-grade goods were still arriving, with an asking price of 16.3 taels, but many were waiting and watching. Spot CW mark was 16 taels, and HM mark was 14 taels. The market was only flat, without surprises, it is said.

Black Pepper and Fragrant Mushroom Markets Both Depressed 167

▲ The removal of black pepper by merchants has been exceptionally sluggish recently. According to overseas telegrams, the Dutch market has fallen by 2.25 guilders. Local firms are eager to sell their stock, but merchant sales are not moving and few traders are interested in buying. Therefore, the market is declining. Yesterday's asking prices were lowered, with "Black Large" at 44 taels and "No. 1" at 45 taels, a decrease of more than one tael compared to the previous session, and few buyers were interested.

▲ The output of new fragrant mushrooms has greatly increased this year. According to reports from Jiangxi, Ningguo, Lanxi, Tunxi, Fujian and other places, the harvest is abundant. Recent arrivals have been very abundant. It is currently estimated that there are more than 500 dan (traditional Chinese unit of dry measure) in stock. However, merchant business is sparse, resulting in an oversupply and falling prices. Currently, good quality large pieces are at 180 taels, high-grade mushrooms are at 168 taels, and ordinary mushrooms are at 160 to 155 taels. There is currently little hope of price increases, it is said.

Shanghai Price Index for April Investigation 168

The National Tariff Commission recently announced the Shanghai price index, saying that since the January 28th Incident, various industries in the city have generally gone on strike, and the wholesale market has almost completely shut down for two months. The Shanghai wholesale, export, and import price indexes compiled by the commission for February and March were both missing. Although the Chamber of Commerce notified on April 1 that it would reluctantly resume business from that day, the Japanese army had not withdrawn, and the Shanghai area was still under military control. Commerce had not yet recovered, and most general prices fell. Comparing the three indexes for April with those for January, exports fell, wholesale prices fell slightly, but imports rose slightly. Opinions

Official Platitudes, Part 3 169

— Buddha

Yesterday's newspaper reported that the Ministry of Interior intends to suggest to the Executive Yuan that future candidates for provincial governors and department heads should be nominated by the central leadership. Those already appointed should also submit detailed resumes for review by the responsible ministry to prevent mediocrity. Is this suggestion a policy to clean up officialdom? Or is it a form of control?

What constitutes mediocrity? What constitutes competence? Since the Xinhai Revolution, the concept of qualifications has long been abandoned. The golden rule of the past, "Don't be an official unless you have someone in court," no longer applies. As long as you have a powerful backer, even mediocrity is not mediocrity. Those who participated in the revolution at some point, even mediocrity is not mediocrity. Or those with a few guns behind them, even mediocrity is not mediocrity. Or those who share the same ideology on a certain condition, even mediocrity is not mediocrity.

Now that the candidates for provincial governors and department heads must be nominated by the central leadership and those already appointed must be reviewed by the responsible ministry, the selection of department heads in the future will be entirely in the hands of the central leadership. What the central leadership considers mediocre is mediocre, and what it considers competent is not mediocre. This is essentially a new system of centralization, not a way to clean up officialdom. Cleaning up officialdom is not done this way.

This is Official Platitudes, Part 3.

Literature and Art

Reflections on Current Events 170

— Ai Shishanfang

Ten thousand insects and sands turned to ashes in the holocaust,

The surviving people still remember the fresh bloodstains.

The earth-shattering quick action became a fleeting memory,

The spirit that pierces the sun relies on a solitary figure.

Singing again the lament of broken vines in the autumn wind,

Just when sparse rain falls on the flower-strewn hour.

From afar, the Chinese descendants think of Jizi,

Sighing that there is no such person in the Central Plains.

Reading History in Anger (Collected Lines from Lu Jiannan) 171

The Guanzhong palace fell into the dust of the enemy,

Brandishing spears, bravely desiring to forget oneself.

The officials in Chang'an are full of worry and fear,

This beautiful land is given to others without resistance.

Abandoned armor lies everywhere on the battlefield,

The autumn wind hunts the yellow Han flags.

The remaining clan sheds tears in the dust of the barbarians,

Helplessly, a fair-faced man seeks peace.

Attending the military headquarters, hunting day after day,

The general pledges allegiance to the country and does not think of returning home.

From now on, cherish the eyes that read books,

There is no one like Yue Fei in the strategic planning.

Moving the capital, how can there be no Guanzhong,

Worries and hardships are like mountains, a smile empties them.

After all, who can distinguish right from wrong,

How many heroes have died in vain throughout history.

Science

Reviving Dry Cell Batteries 172

— Gong

The use of electricity and the progress of the world are always directly proportional. The more the world progresses, the more electricity is used. Therefore, in recent decades, the use of electricity has increased day by day. Dry cell batteries are one example. Flashlights, small radios, and other machines that require little electricity all use them. But one thing is a pity: if a dry cell battery is used up in a day, it's useless and you have to buy a new one, which is very uneconomical. Now there is a way to make used dry cell batteries work again. I'll write this method below:

Dissolve ammonium chloride in a bowl of warm water to make a saturated solution (that is, pour ammonium chloride into the water and stir with a stick until it is completely dissolved in the water or completely disappears, then add more ammonium chloride and stir until it can no longer dissolve in the water). Then, take the used dry cell battery with the case intact. Make several holes in its case, then put it in this solution for several hours. Take it out, and it will have electricity again. I have tried this method several times. Although the revived dry cell battery doesn't last as long as a new one, it is much cheaper than buying a new one. Finally, I must state that when putting it in the solution, do not let the carbon rod in the middle touch the solution. If it does, it will be useless.

School Announcements

Ten Minutes Before Class 173

— Ganniu

In classroom two of S University, it was nine o'clock, ten minutes before class. Several college students were talking.

"Old Li, you didn't go to class yesterday afternoon? Did you go to the movies with Miss Chen? That little bird's hips are very developed, she looks too fat," said Ah Huang, the optimist.

Then, Xiao Hei, the radical with the nickname "Little Black," said angrily, "In this time of national crisis, you are still indulging in love? We should rise up and do our best to fight the enemy, sacrificing ourselves for the country!"

Before Xiao Hei finished speaking, Wen Bin, a bookworm of the scholar class, said with a sneer, "You people only shout slogans and don't do anything practical. Have you ever done anything for the benefit of the country or society? Our only responsibility now is to study. We can ignore all national affairs."

"That's a joke! You don't care if the country is destroyed? Where will you go to study? The country is an organization that protects the people, and the people should uphold the dignity of the country," said Zhou, a petty bureaucrat.

"You always talk about the country, what has the country given us? What benefits have we gained?" Xiao Yichen, the pessimist, said indifferently.

Before anyone could say anything else, the bell for class rang, and everyone stopped talking.

Idle Theories

Her Disappointment 174

— Wu

"Mom! I want four dimes worth of foreign stamps." Qin Fang had just returned from school and was already finding her mother to act coy.

"Oh? How many letters do you have to send?"

"It's not that. There's a really good lipstick advertised in the newspaper. If you send four dimes, they'll send you a sample box. Lingying, from the Li family, has already written and sent a letter. I want to too."

"Go ask your father for it. It's okay for a young lady to put on a little lipstick."

× × ×

The third day, she was holding the telephone receiver at school.

"Are you Mr. Wang? ... I'm Qin! ... See a movie? See a movie? ... I'm not going this afternoon. ... Why? ... Sorry! ... So, will you go tomorrow? ... Hehehe ... Thank you! ... Goodbye! ... Goodbye!"

She hung up the phone. She was really angry. She thought, "Why hasn't the lipstick been sent yet? Not putting on any lipstick and going to see a movie with a man; what is that? Maybe it will be sent tomorrow. ... I really let him down today!"

× × ×

Time passed quickly, and it was the second third day again.

In the classroom, the teacher was lecturing on the platform, but she was whispering with Lingying.

"Has your lipstick been sent?"

"Not yet. What about yours?"

"It hasn't been sent either."

"So, why?"

"I think it's probably a scam to get stamps. Do you think so?"

"That's right! I think so too. I'm so angry!"

So that's how it was. She really felt sorry for her Mr. Wang a few days ago. As for the forty cents worth of stamps? What a waste!

Street Scenes and Alleyways

Records of Street Observations 175

— Yuxian

What is Shanghai? There is no need to use a lot of words and language to explain it. As long as you study everything you see on the street, you will get a correct answer.

I have seen a loafer carrying a beggar with broken feet on his back in the morning, placing him at a busy street corner, and then carrying him back in the evening. If you want to study their relationship, it must be nothing more than father and son, or brothers.

I have seen a mother and son pretending to be a ship's steward and a passenger, arguing over a piece of luggage behind the Great World entertainment complex. The son said she didn't pay for the boat, and the mother said she couldn't find her relatives, and he was stealing her luggage.

Of course, writing complaints on the ground is also a common occurrence. I saw a five- or six-year-old child writing on the sidewalk with chalk, "Orphaned child XXX, lost parents early..." and other clichéd complaints. Many people were gathered around. Although everyone knew that the child was a cunning character, some people still threw him a few coppers. Because the child's writing was very beautiful, I also threw him a silver dime. The Shanghainese people around me looked at me with strange eyes, as if saying, "What a waste! Is it worth throwing away a silver dime for this!"

Shanghainese people have no sympathy or pity, only black eyeballs and white silver dollars. Is Shanghai really like this? Please go to the streets and search for the answer.

Looking Through the Western Mirror

Letting the Cat Out of the Bag 176

— T

A certain wealthy merchant was hosting a dinner, and the guest of honor was a certain division commander. The wealthy merchant was flattering the commander, praising him effusively.

The commander said with a sigh, "The ways of the world are so fickle these days..."

"Yes," the wealthy merchant interrupted before the commander could finish, "Who these days isn't just a fair-weather friend? Are there any truly loyal people left? Only..."

He paused for a moment and continued, "To be honest, only our XXX flatterer can be considered a loyal person. As long as there's a connection, not to mention anything else, just talking about you, commander..."

"Not to curse the commander, but even if the commander became a beggar and came to my place, I would still treat him the same way I do today," he said.

"Hey! Why are you cursing the commander? Forgive me! Forgive me! I deserve to be slapped!" He said, slapping himself twice. The commander nodded, seemingly paying attention but not really caring.

"XXX is here again. Does the master want to see him?" The doorman came in and said this.

"Hmph! That pauper is here again? You wait, I'll chase him away!" The wealthy merchant replied sternly.

"XXX? Isn't that the former Commander X of the X Division of the X Army? What happened to him after he fell from grace?" The commander asked, reminiscing.

"Him? He's not good himself. How can he have the commander's good fortune? And he often comes here to borrow money. Who has money to lend him? Now he's practically a beg...gar..." He said, his face turning red without realizing it.

"Oh..." The commander smiled silently.

A Corner of Society

A Maid's Autobiography (Part 1) 177

— Leshan

Last Sunday, at the residence of my old friend Mr. C, I heard the newly hired maid recount the hellish life she lived as a servant in the S residence three years ago. I thought that cases of maid abuse are still heard from time to time these days, so I specifically wrote it out to tell the general advocates of humanitarianism and the emancipation of slaves and servants:

I (the maid's self-description, and so on below) and XX were both unfortunately sold by our parents, who were forced by hunger and cold, to the S residence to work as maids. After being fed by them, although my (body and hair) were (received from my parents), at that time they were (received from the master). They could beat or scold me, making me their slave.

My former employer had a master, mistress, young master, young lady, young master's wife, and the young lady's daughter, a little girl. Although there were only six people, cooking and serving tea was very difficult. It was truly a case of "the master wants wontons, the mistress wants noodles." What suited the master's taste did not suit the mistress's preferences. Therefore, we were often scolded and annoyed, and even beaten.

The master and the young master's wife were both addicted to opium. Lying on the couch, they often wanted us to massage their legs until the middle of the night. We had to keep our sleepy eyes open and massage their legs. I remember once when XX fell asleep while massaging because she was tired, the young mistress stabbed her with the burning opium pipe support, causing her to scream like a slaughtered pig. To this day, the image of her bleeding remains deeply in my mind.

Especially on those cold winter nights when the north wind was blowing fiercely, when the masters gave the order to eat a midnight snack, we had to get up from our warm blankets. Although we trembled with cold, we finally braced ourselves and braved the cold to do it.

The seventeen- or eighteen-year-old young master was the most mischievous and violent. He often condescended to fight us, and when he was happy, he would put his arms around us and kiss us, insulting us at will. When he was unhappy, he would punch and kick us. The most unjust thing was when the masters saw it, they would always whip us without asking why, accusing us of seducing the young master. We really had no way to explain ourselves!

Later, we naturally avoided this harmful young master like snakes and scorpions. However, he became angry out of shame and picked on us. He would either say that the tea was cold or that the water was too hot. I remember one summer morning, XX invited him to wash his face. She invited him three times before he graced us with his presence, but he scolded her for the water being cold. XX added some hot water, but unexpectedly it scalded his precious hand. He suddenly splashed the basin of water on XX, drenching her completely. The thin summer clothes clung tightly to her body. This cruel young master clapped his hands and laughed, shouting, "Look at the model..." She was so ashamed that she wanted to find a hole to hide in.

Nonsense

The Dominance of (Old Sayings) 178

— Yunzong

Speaking of the situation in our country, everyone knows that it is terribly bad. Although there have been several reforms recently, it's just changing the soup without changing the medicine, with different names but the same reality. Internal and external troubles come one after another, the country is weak and the people are poor, and the future is bleak. As I see it, the reason for this is that a few (old sayings) are dominating the situation. Don't you believe it? Please see:

1. (Each person sweeps the snow from their own doorstep, and doesn't care about the frost on others' roofs.) From then on, everyone is selfish and only knows themselves, harming the public for their own benefit. National affairs are not worth asking about.

2. (If you are not in the position, do not meddle in its affairs.) From then on, even if those in power act arbitrarily and commit all kinds of evil, everyone still bows their heads and acts as obedient citizens. How can the country have a new atmosphere?

3. (Moving once is worse than staying still.) From then on, people stick to the old ways and hate reform. Other cultures are progressing rapidly, but we can't catch up. How can we resist them?

4. (Leave everything to fate, don't force it.) From then on, the rich just celebrate their wealth, and the poor just endure their poverty. Everyone lacks the spirit of brave struggle and upward effort, resulting in a stagnant, backward nation that is subject to being slaughtered by others.

5. (Of the three unfilial acts, having no descendants is the greatest.) Even those who are so poor that they can barely afford to defecate hope for many sons and grandsons, so that the family line continues. From then on, there are too many people and not enough food, and everyone fights for food, making the situation even more unstable.

Only when no one believes in the old sayings above will China stand out.

Movies

Chaplin's Drawing Strength from Imaginary Plums 179

After the news of Mr. Chaplin's arrival in Shanghai was announced, the general public has been eagerly awaiting him. However, Mr. Chaplin is still delaying his trip. Recently, he went to Japan from Hong Kong. According to Chaplin's interview with Hong Kong reporters, he said that his three most satisfying works are "The Circus", "City Lights", and "The Big Adventure". The first two films are well known to the people of Shanghai. The third film is a satire of society, which has now been purchased by the Paris Theater in this city for a large sum of money and translated into "Street Hero". It is scheduled to be screened on the 18th (today). Those who admire Chaplin can use this to "draw strength from imaginary plums." Chaplin's art in this film is like the rising sun, shining brightly. Its grand situation should not be less than "City Lights".

(5) Execution Clerk: Zhu Guangzhao; Process Server: Ying Shengsan

▲Public Notice Regarding Public Service

Having investigated, in the case of Stobert and Shunxingchang regarding a goods debt, because the defendant Shunxingchang's whereabouts are unknown, documents cannot be served. Based on the plaintiff's petition for public service, it has been ruled and approved, and lawyer Cao Xuanzhang has been appointed as the defendant's special agent. The court has now set the date for a public hearing at 2:00 PM on June 9th in the court's 10th courtroom. The summons that the defendant should receive is hereby publicly served according to the law. The defendant should comply and attend the hearing on time to defend themselves, and must not delay. This public service is hereby issued.

The above is for the defendant Shunxingchang to note.

▲Regarding Public Service

Having investigated, in the case of China Exchange Bank versus Wu Qizhou et al. regarding a debt, previously, because the defendant Ge Zhongliang's whereabouts were unknown, the original judgment could not be served. Subsequently, based on the plaintiff bank's petition for public service, it has been ruled and approved. The original judgment that the defendant should receive is hereby publicly served according to Article 184 of the Civil Procedure Law.

The above is for the defendant Ge Zhongliang to note.

▲Regarding Public Service

Having investigated, in the case of Hu Detai versus Zhang Guangtai regarding rent arrears, previously, because the defendant Zhang Guangtai's whereabouts were unknown, the original judgment could not be served. Subsequently, based on the plaintiff Hu Detai's petition for public service, it has been ruled and approved. The original judgment that the defendant should receive is hereby publicly served according to Article 184 of the Civil Procedure Law.

The above is for the defendant Zhang Guangtai to note.
